How cool is that? I could probably use my warhammer40k minis for this, too. This game would be great for anyone who would like a miniature wargame that is light, easy, relatively short and inexpensive, and doesn't require arts and crafts skills (or just doesn't have the time for it, anymore).

RATING: 10
There's more strategy to this game than people give it credit for.  Those who disagree haven't played it enough, because I felt the same way initially.  

There absolutely is a lot of dice rolling, but what about the glyphs? height advantages? movement advantages? army construction?  You can easily win or lose based upon good and bad tactical decisions.

It's lighter than the hardcore minis games for sure, but it's also more fun and cheaper.

RATING: 6
Truly a toy with wonderful plastic terrain - which has been begging to be made for years. The game is a basic move-roll-attack-repeat affair with some mixed in special rules for the figures. Nothing unexpected at all. Not that I actually *play* the game by the rules. Oh, I've done that once or twice. But the better game is with our own rules - combining Mage Knight figures which adds a boat load of strategy - which this game desperately needs. Get it for the glorious bits. Don't get it for the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I love this game. The only thing preventing me from playing it every day is that set up and clean up take FOREVER. Usually we will set up a map and leave it out on the table for a few weeks and get lots of plays in before we have to deal with the arduous process of putting it away. 

The base set includes enough for several different scenarios and there are some good map suggestions included. If you get more tiles and characters you can create your own maps and scenarios and strategy will change depending on the armies you pick. 

I really enjoy the gameplay of the master version over the basic game since it adds special attacks and hitpoints so strategy needs to be greatly changed. Basic is a great starter for kids or people who are difficult to teach, but master is where it shines.

I own 2 of the master set and several expansions and character sets.

RATING: 9
Sheer gaming bliss.

[i]This[/i] is the AT game I've been looking for. It plays fast, it's got simple rules, it lends itself to some strategy, it's infinitely variable and configurable. It's got dice dice dice and luck luck luck. 

I mean, where else can you have your zombie army charge into battle behind a pack of flayed plague dogs, backed up by a squad of Redcoats, an acid-spitting dragon, and a railgun-toting robot? To combat the U.S. Airborne, a squad of cybernetically enhanced gorillas, Captain America, a squad of Roman archers, and a pack of wolves? It's tabletop madness. 

[b][i]Brilliance![/b][/i]

RATING: 8
Rating is based on my buddy's collection and he has just about everything.

This is not the best game in the world, but it is by far the coolest.  Why?  Because in my first game, I had a hoard of zombies fighting alongside soldiers from the American Revolution and a squad of U.S. Paratroopers.  I was going up against Hellhounds, Elven archers, and the Men in Black.

Nuff said.  This is this coolest game ever.

I know: you are supposed to coordinate your units so their special abilities work with each other.  Ho hum.  This game is about picking pieces based on how cool they look, having a crazy (yet very simple battle) and then telling stories about it months later.  It is all that is good in gaming.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Don't judge this by it's cover. It may be suitable for kids, but it's much more than that. 
This is the perfect skirmish game: I can explained it in minutes, and everyone can play without consulting the rulebook afterwards. Best of all: the expansions add variety, but the Master set still has the great units, it's not just a starter-kit. People that are complaining about luck of the dice have not played enough. Luck is a factor but it's more important to choose the right units, position them optimally and activate them at the right time. Don't just play last man standing though, that's a slugfest in every game, play a good scenario or CTF.

RATING: 8
Le retour des petits des avec des cranes.
Ce bon vieux systeme de heroquest est toujours en vie!

Beaux jeux, pleins d'expensions et de possibilites.  Le board est un puzzle hexagonal sur lesquelles les pieces se deplacent pour s'affronter a celles de l'adversaire.   Il y a plusieurs scenarios et conditions de victoire. 

La magie est dans la collection des differents personnages qui ont leur propres statistiques, forces et faiblesses et dans leur utilisation strategique en fonction de leur utilite et de le cout.  

Une partie dure de une a deux heures.

RATING: 8
Miniatures games do not get any more accessible than this. The box has an assortment of miniatures and their cards from different factions, glyphs for power-ups, turn markers, dice and tiles for creating 3D maps. The rules for combat and movement are easy to follow, yet not oversimplified and feature a number of scenarios that keep the game interesting.

RATING: 6
After a nice 6 month grace period of owning this game, the intial glee I got from all the nice bits and pieces seems to have worn off. The gameplay on this one, while fun and lighthearted, is rather lacking. Unit drafting is predictable. The play is controlled predominately by luck. I would suggest it as a light non-gamer game, but in my opinion the set-up time, the pricetag, and the storage space required for this one bring it down a notch.

RATING: 10
This game is one of the few, rare perfect 10 scores I will likely ever offer. The reasons are many but this game seems to fit my desire for a game to be simple, to incorporate miniatures, and to be new each time it is played. With all the expansions, many still readily available, this game is almost assured to never be the same game twice.

This game is just great. Its only drawback is that the just the core game itself is not enough to play - oh it technically is, but you'll quickly realize that you wont be happy playing on a flat board. You'll want rises and cliffs and hills. I dont deduct a point for this (whereas I do for other games that are not complete in the box) because it is NOT expensive to pick up some additional terrain.

RATING: 7.5
I have this game as the base game, plus some additional units and land/castle tiles from booster packs & expansions.  This game is amazingly innovative, and packs the flare to surprise your standard RPG expectations.  It has simple rules for kids, but the real game is with the advanced rules.  While the rules aren't anything to write home about (more dice rolling, and hit points, etc), the fact that the scenarios, playing fields, castles (expansion), and general landscape are entirely customizable is genius.  Combining the thrill of legos, with RPG wars.  Where it stumbles is all the stuff after that, the rules are sometimes messy, and combat is surprisingly not innovative or inspired.  And therefor the game is a one trick-pony, but a good one trick pony at that.

RATING: 9.5
If this had came out when I was a boy, I think my whole childhood would be different. This is the game that I've always wanted to play. Simple rules. All sorts of different guys beating each other up. And an almost lego-like map system for creating your own maps.
Things I don't like about the game:
1) Takes a while to set up a map. I'll usually have to set up a map ahead of time and leave it out. Custom maps are fun to make, but it's a lot of work to make them balanced for a really good game. 2) Would be nice if there were more ways to win, rather than just beating each other up. Again, you can make a custom scenario, but it takes work to make it balanced. 3) I've spent a lot of money on it. It's probably about half of the value of my total boardgame collection, but it doesn't come close to half of the playing time. Although, once my boys are older, I'm sure it will get a lot more play.

Edit: Bumped rating down a little bit. Lately, I've been wanting to play things like Monsterpocalypse instead of this.

Edit again: rating bumped back up. Kids are older now and we play this almost every chance we get. The maps still take a long time to set up, but we build them together and have a lot of fun with it. We don't worry about making it balanced. Just make something interesting and try it out.

RATING: 8
MiniaturesGame, Solo

The rules are simple, the terrain is great, and the armies are crazy.  It's a dicefest, but it's a strangely enjoyable dicefest.... and the components are great.  Looking forward to the expansion, whenever I can get it.  I actually have two copies of the game, which is enough for me.  I am considering a third copy....

Even if I never got the expansions, this game would have a lot of replay value.  Sometimes I even regret getting the expansions, due to a desire for simplicity, but they certainly don't hurt!  Great for kids young and old.  ;)

RATING: 6
Universal combat game, where anything can fight anything, you just give it an attack, defence, move and range value, a size and decide any special rules that may apply.

You need a lot of terrain to make a large battlefield or achieve any relief, as the rules account for things 25 rows high, which is hard to do unless you buy lots of stuff!

Pretty simple game tho and the very nice, prepainted figures that come with the game mean that it is definitely a way to get kids in to the progression from "toy soldiers" to using a simple ruleset.

RATING: 7
My rating for this has nothing to do with the actual game, and everything to do with the game pieces as being useful for using in other systems.

There are people that will torch me for this, but I think the Heroscape game mechanics stink. I have yet to play a game where it didn't come down to the dice being finicky in one person's favor and screwing the other.

After a 45 minute set-up time I think that's a bit like flipping off a box of kittens. Just plain wrong.

I love the concept, production values, and pieces, but the game itself annoys the crap out of me. I have been trying for 3 years to come up with an adequate mod of the rules to satisfy the Battletech / Twilight Struggle fan in me and make it less about luck and more about strategy.

If anyone has any suggestions, please feel free to PM them to me.

RATING: 8
The figs and terrain are really, really cool.  Feels like a 12 year old's dream toy - I wish I had had this game as a kid.  The game itself is a combination of obvious moves and not-so-obvious moves.  There is often a best fig, and you pile all your order tokens on him and blast away at your opponent.  However, since you place order markers and then roll initiative, you have to plan for the possibility of going second or first.  This is where the decisions, such as they are, come in.  Drafting is also quite strategic, with lots of good decisions and counter decisions.  Ultimately, the game is not deep, but can be appreciated for what it is: a light hack and slash affair with great bits.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Same comments for my Marvel Heroscape set:

Great game, simple rules.  Love the simplicity of this system and the way the special powers manage to capture the essence of the theme.  Great fun!

There may not be much terrain in the base box, I bought two as they can be found quite cheaply, it is worth it - I am also looking at using this game at school, the kids would be wild about a game that is about this subject let alone a game that looks the way this one looks.

The simplicity of the game is a real bonus, everything in the game, from moving up, fighting and special powers are all logically handled within this simple framework.

The role of dice in this game is profound, if you are the sort of player who is turned off by a significant amount of luck then this is a game that you would be better off avoiding, however, if you can live with this strong element of luck this game is thematic and a rollicking adventure.  The best part is it doesn't outstay it's welcome.

Rise of the Valkyrie is a great set because it contains a fantastic mix of units, from heroes to squads, as well as a massive amount of terrain - very much worthwhile!!

I'd also go ahead and skip the basic rules and jump right in with the full rules. I don't see it getting much play with only a single set, but I can see how multiple sets and the many expansions could lead to a much more interesting game with lots more variety in the scenarios.

UPDATE: My son pulled it out this summer, built a couple of scenarios, and he and his dad really enjoyed it.  It's back up to an 8.

UPDATE 7-30-12: Man, I really need to sell this system.  It takes up massive space in our house and we never play it.  I have so many base sets and expansions, it's ridiculous!  I look back on a comment I made from a couple of years ago about keeping it simple, and I highly recommend that.  You can have plenty of fun with one base set and maybe a few extras.  Don't get roped in by all the crazy pictures of scenarios you see online.  Play the base at least 10 times. If you feel the need to expand, do it gradually.

RATING: 8
Initial rating of "9." With about 2 years of gaming under my belt, I was suspicious that I was a relative Eurogamer "centrist." Sure, there are a few oddball games that I really enjoy, but for the most part, the few classic "Ameritrash" games that I played left me underwhelmed.

If Heroscape is Ameritrash, then I am totally on board. This is fun, hilarious, absurd in its total genre mish-mash, and fairly strategic. There's a bit of "deckbuilding" with your army construction, a bit of Memoir '44 with the army movement and dice rolling... it's just a wonderful blend of figures and gaming.

Thank goodness I have a close couple/friends that have fully invested in this game. I can't see myself ever picking this up, but I'm more than happy to help them get as much mileage out of this game as I can.

RATING: 6

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Revised comment- original follows!

A couple of years on, and my enthusiam for HEROSCAPE has waned a lot- tons of expansions, new figures from every nook and cranny of the imagination, gamers using 2, 3, 4, 5 sets to make gigantic, floor-covering games...yet somehow I feel that as a game HEROSCAPE never really met its potential to develop into a more comprhensive and progressively complex system.  The new figures add new abilities and a couple of kinks but ultimately gameplay returns to the same things we were doing when the game first came out.  Don't get me wrong- I still think HEROSCAPE is a lot of fun, and I still believe that the game has likely birthed a new generation of gamers in the basements and dining rooms of the world but I rarely feel driven to play the game any more myself despite its significance.  I still rate it high, and I'm glad to jump in on a pickup game from time to time but I can't help but think that the game should have expanded "up" more than "out".
>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
After several sessions, this is definitely a 10,I can see playing this for a long time to come.  This game is something else, possibly even "important"...congratulations to the Daviau/Van Ness/Baker team for getting this published and onto store shelves- Walmart has never seen anything quite like this.  Yes, a game with line-of-sight and terrain rules has arrived in mainstream retailers.  What's next? ZOCs and CRTs?  This is the perfect way to introduce "hobby" gaming to a mass audience- it's attractive, different, and at just the right complexity level to both attract new players and interest veterans.  Gameplay is amazingly simple (just a few steps up from Epic Duels) but the fun factor is through the roof.  Kids will play this game and remember it fondly 15 years from now.  Oh, and it features amazing miniatures.  My eyes popped out when I opened the box.  Can't wait for the Romans!    
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.3
I've played this about seven or eight times over the past year with my sons ages 7 and 10, and it has been ok, but at times it has felt like a simple probability test without a lot of choices to make.  Last night I played with a colleague from work.  We alternated turns building the map a piece at a time, then chose four interesting glyphs and randomly placed them on the board.

It was a blast!  I used Throgrim and another piece for defensive bonuses for Sylvarrus (sp), who kept trying to stop the crushing onslaught of the Zettian guards.  I sent my Samurai around the ruins to slice and dice the paratroopers, who were lobbing grenades at Thorgrim.  A lone viking stood guard on a  1 attack glyph and my remaining samurai tried to dislodge him to no avail.  Meanwhile Johnny Shotgun was picking off my krav maga agents with his six shooter, getting incredibly thematic dice roles.  Finally, the Marro meat puppets began regenerating and although I came very close Syvarrus could not detonate the Zettians.

Lessons learned: The paratroopers roll to enter the board every *round* not every turn.  Also, don't judge a game you've only played against young kids.  Finally, choose really good scenarios with objectives.

update: we have so many expansions that the thought of setting this up is exhausting.

Another update: We had this in storage when we went overseas for two years and it was great to break it out when we returned!

RATING: 8
Imagine if you will the lone remaining, and frightened Guilty McCreech as he looks over a battle-scarred field of his slain comrades. His head hangs. His gaze lingers on the chamber of his revolver. Only one bullet left. He grits his teeth. A tear. Suddenly, filled with a bloodlusty, blind rage brought forth from the torture of his ancestors Genghis Khan and Vlad the Impaler's souls which have sat dormant for thousands of years in the void, whips out is 6-shooter,and surgically bounces a bullet off of a rock face and threads it through a thicket of trees! The bullet pierces a stalking Dragon right in the eye and passes through the dragon's cerebral cortex, halting all hopes of motor abilities he might have once enjoyed. Guilty, jumps from atop the tree (that he obviously force-jumped to the top of) and wrenches the dragon's head off for good measure. He holds the head high and bathes in a cascade of the lifeblood of ancient magics. He pulls out the bullet in the dragons brain stem with his teeth. He grabs his junk and blows a kiss at the crumpled dragon-heap.

A rustling from above. A Shaolin Monk descends from the tree. Hand-to-hand combat ensues. Guilty is losing ground. No, not this way. He's come to far. He rips a mighty oak from its roots. Not unlike the way a giant circus tent stake is driven into the ground, Guilty heaves the oak atop the monk's head. The monk dodges, but not fast enough. The monk is pinned neck down beneath the mighty tree. Guilty's boot spur clanks into view. He crouches low, with the bullet still wet in dragon blood in his hand. Slowly, Guilty forces the bullet into the temple of the twitching monk. 

What's that? A glint of light atop a cliff face miles in the distance? Ah, it's the scope flair of the deadliest sniper of all time, Deadeye Dan. Guilty is in his sights. Not to worry, Guilty slowly retrieves the bullet from the monk, he stares defiantly  at where the glint of light came from. And in a very "I could give a damn" type of manner, guilty lobs the bullet high in the air and turns his back. It's been a long day. Guilty lights a cigarette with the dragon's heat glands. It's a long tasty drag off of the cig. He walks away from the cliff into the trees. He deserves some XXX Whiskey. He's gone. 

In the hazy distance, against the rocky backdrop of the cliff, we see a limp, lifeless black dot in free fall...


(THIS is my experience with this game. Never have I been more excited to lose a game several hours in the making. This game is so addictively fun. It's a game that you can get so involved in that every blow and victory feels like a personal tragedy and success respectively.)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Plus expansions

This may very well be the perfect game. The only reason I haven't played this in over a year is due to the fact that I had immersed myself in it for more than 2 years at the expense of all the other games in my collection, and I really wanted to get to those.

The minis and terrain are gorgeous, the units are incredibly varied and feel true to the characters they represent, the game has a perfect blend of strategy and luck, the game is easy to teach, and the game system is flexible enough to handle pretty much any house rules and customs you can throw at it.

Heroscapers.com is one of the friendliest and most talented communities on the Internet, and they have enhanced and expanded the system beyond imagination, particularly with respect to superhero customs.

One quip: I >hate< the weird 7-hex tile size of the cards in the game. Thankfully there are rectangular sized cards available.

RATING: 8
Heroscape looks absolutely mind blowing when compared to most board games. The 3D terrain is terrific and the pre-painted figures are very high quality. A fully set up game of Heroscape makes most other board games look dreadfully boring. So, very high toy factor here. The rules are very simple. It takes a few minutes to learn and then you can start playing. But while the rules are simple the gameplay still retains a good amount of both strategic and tactical depth. I recommend Heroscape for people who can handle and enjoy randomness and are looking for a great looking game that is as fun to set up as it is to play.

RATING: 10
I arrived far too late to this one from a cost perspective -- only made worse with the discontinuation announcement -- but what an amazing game. 

Can be played in so many variations: All the way from specific scenarios to theme-vs-theme battles to team vs team contests or massive free-for-alls. There's even the ultra-competitive tourney scene. Fans of strategy, wargaming, abstracts, and/or heavily themed Ameritrash can all find something to enjoy here. There are even those who buy the master sets just for the terrain and contruct phenomenal maps that are practically works of art. It really is a game that can be all things for *most* people (not quite all...those whose taste strictly favors eurogames need not apply).

**Have updated to a 10. Any game that has me thinking about it all day long shouldn't be rated any less. It's officially my desert island game.

The game itself is a dull coin flip livened by beautiful figures and complex terrain.  The only interesting mecahnic is having to plan the next three turns ahead of time. A game that is kinda fun to play, but that doesn't grab you and make you think about it all hours of the night is the definition of a 6.

Update: After a few more plays this has to get lowered from a 6 to a 4.  Without overwatch or damage sloped over range or _something_ interesting, this game will sit on my shelf for the rest of time.  (Until the aforementioned BattleTech campaign starts.)

Updatex2: After playing Battletech with the actual full set of official maps, this terrain system is shown to be incapable of handling terrain complex enough to be fun.  Lowering from a 4 to a 2.  This is junk.

RATING: 3
Sadly, one of the most interesting things about this game keeps it from seeing much table time: the interlocking terrain.  Set-up time is just waaay too long and trying to assemble a terrain "board" from the step-by-step guide for the published scenarios is tedious!!  

If I want to play this, it has to be at my house (I can't lug all this stuff to other folks' homes) and I need at least 30 minutes of "quiet time" to throw a board together.

The well-painted (for mass market) figures are really nice, as is the price for the stuff at big-box stores!

I've got a major quibble with one of the rules (height advantage), but other than that, a fair, LITE game.  I think it's the collector in me that enjoys the game; it's certainly not the rules as they are dicefest-central.

UPDATE: SOLD MY COLLECTION!!  Yes, I'm excited- I freed up 8 cubic feet of space in my house by doing so!!  Good grief!!  I can't help now but to look upon my former love affair with this game as, well, a bit...silly...

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
One of my all time favourite games and one that I think is very close (for me anyways) to mechanical perfection. The combat dice and order markers ensure that while a the better player and the one who pulls ahead will generally get the win, the player who falls behind and even is down to his last unit is still in the game and stands a chance of winning. Add onto that the point system for building armies and the very flexible terrain means you have a very deep game and never have to play the same situation twice.

I only have a couple (relatively) minor complaints. First is unless a melee unit has some sort of ability that gives it a boost versus ranged unit, it can be a bit too easy for the ranged units to destroy the melee before the melee can engage. Second, because common units essentially treat all squads as part of the same card, common units do not lose effectiveness as easily a unique units do (since a single unique kill reduces the number of figures you take a turn with instantly while the commons are not affected this way until they have less than one squad's worth of figures left). Finally, I wish the game had a little bit more hidden information involved beyond the order markers and glyphs.

Note, this rating and comment applies to Heroscape as a whole. I have a number of packs and expansions that I did not bother adding or rating.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Bought 9/3/04. After two plays it rated a 9. A very FUN game. Certainly not a serious strategy game, but when taken as fun, it is a most enjoyable game and the terrain and miniatures add immensely to the value of the game. This game recalls the kind of game I dreamed of as a youth.
However...after playing it 6 times it is getting a bit burdensome to 1) set up, 2) draft, 3) put up. Thus, a one hour game actually takes closer to two hours - especially if setting up a 2 or more set game. Tonight it took us over an hour to set up the game (2 sets) & draft - 2 hours to play (3 players) - and 45 minutes to put up - a total of nearly 5 hours! We started at 6:30 and finished around 11:30. Though the game was fun, tense, and exciting - we felt we were "missing out" on the rest of the gaming in the room (5 games were played while we played one)! Thus - I dropped it back to an 8.

RATING: 4.5
I love minis games, and have played Heroscape maybe ten times.  It's inexpensive and fun to play with kids.  Beyond that, this game is hugely overrated.  No possible way to customize gear or weapons on any unit.  Typically one special ability for each unit on its recipe card, and that's it.  Every single model in the game hits and auto-wounds on a 4+ and has a 5+ ward save.  Annoying plastic hex legos to set up & put away.  If you are used to playing other miniatures games, you will find this way too boring.  It's not a terrible game.  It's just that pretty much every other minis game is better.

RATING: 6
Oh Heroscape. I so wanted to like you! Stephen Baker, it was you who invented HeroQuest, one of my first and favourite games. Battle Masters was next, and while light in strategy it was heavy in theme and plastic. Heroscape looked beautiful all set up. The theme behind it is pretty weak, but so what. However, with all the arbitrary special powers and mish-mash of characters, I just couldn't get into it as much as I wanted. When you boil it down, Heroscape is just another game where you throw dice at each other and keep your fingers crossed. Yes, those who memorize all of the characters' special powers and can manipulate their own special powers enough will be victorious. This takes a lot of game play. For those who are into light miniatures games, I can see why they love this. But I don't have the patience to learn the fine points of this game when in the end it's just a dicefest. When I play a dicefest, I don't want to have to know the game system like it was kin; I just wanna set up my pieces, and go gung ho on my opponent until they're bleeding. 10 out of 10 for component wow factor, but I think I'll stick with Battle Masters if I want mindless dice-kills, and HeroQuest if I want a richer theme.

RATING: 10
Fun game with 2 or more people.  Rated it lower though because of cost + time to set up.  Also, as of this date, Heroscape is no longer in print.  Prices are even more elevated now.

Update: 3.11.13
I've had this for years now, started collecting it in 2007 or so.  Played it a lot early on--when there were friends to play along.  When I first got on bgg I rated it lower (6) because of the pain of setting up.  After returning to it, I'm raising the rating from 6 to 7 because even though set up is a pain, it really is such a good game when you get one set up.  Very unique.  

Update 7.26.14
Continues to see the table on a regular basis, and it continues to prove that it deserves to be up there with some of the best.  Changing the rating back up to an 8.  The set up issues I shared earlier can be alleviated by playing smaller maps, which the more I play, that's where I think the sweet spot is.

Update: 3.12.16
Okay, after years of play, and playing hundreds of other games I still just have a blast playing this and believe it deserves a nearly perfect rating because of that.  Plays so smoothly and virtually flawlessly.

RATING: 8
[Original comment] I have played three games of this, two with 2 players and one with 3 players. I think it has the feel of chess on a more expansive scale. I see that this is going to be a classic, with all the potential for expansions, modifications, home-created scenarios, etc. It appears the future for this game is almost limitless. The 3-player game I participated in included a 7-year-old, a 36-year-old, and a 61-year-old, and we all equally enjoyed it. In fact, the final battle was between the 7 and 61 guys, with equal heroes. May 2009 -- I do not own this game and haven't played it for the past four years, but it is an interesting game system.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Another incomplete game, this is one of those titles that only get better the more you spend on it.  Even though this older master set has more pieces than the current master sets, its still not really enough to get the full potential out of this game.  

The game itself makes for a good light war game and I think if I owned many more sets, it would be much more a blast and more epic.  If this was the case I think I prefer this game over Memoir '44.  There are no cards to this game and I think this is a rare case where this game is better for it compared to Memoir '44.  I like card-driven wargames, they usually add much to the flavor of wargames, but in Memoir the card play is just a command mechanic and add nothing to flavor, but this game of Heroescape, skips that pretense and gets straight into the game.  

The 3D nature and variations in terrain is a boon also.  The game mechanics are simple compare to the usual grognard fare, but they simple work and work well.  

If I was to invest in this system now, I would do well to buy a large used collect with several master sets.  The new sets based on D&D are more expensive and you get %25 less tiles.

The few sets I own now, I can't rate this game more than memoir, which play better out of the initial box.  I am sure that will change if I ever decide to invest more in this system.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Un juego ya descatalogado que, considerado en el contexto adecuado, está francamente bien. Más allá de su espectacularidad visual -tablero modular que permite mil y una combinaciones y decenas de miniaturas pintadas de guerreros históricos y fantásticos- tiene unas mecánicas inteligentes que funcionan muy bien.

Los diseñadores han creado un juego de batallas fantásticas en el que prima el dinamismo y en el que las reglas jamás son un obstáculo, sino una útil herramienta. La clave o que hace diferente este juego y le da todo su potencial son las características particulares y las habilidades especiales de las miniaturas, y la forma en que interactúan unas con otras.

Si añadimos que los jugadores pueden reclutar libremente sus fuerzas -lo que es bastante divertido de por si-, que el juego admite hasta 4 jugadores (o 6 si se dispone de dos copias, tenemos un estupendo entretenimiento que difícilmente defraudará.

Dos últimas salvedades: que quede claro que el juego es lo que es, y no hay que buscar en él profundidad estratégica ni simulación elevada; no es ese su objetivo. Y por su propia idiosincrasia, el factor azar es muy elevado.

RATING: 9
Went nuts and bought a huge amount of Heroscape in spring 2011. Three base sets owned plus the terrain from a fourth.

After a couple of plays I realised that the characters in the base set are all you need. The game is actually more fun when you have a tighter set of balanced characters that you're reasonably familiar with. So I sold off most of my other characters and focussed on getting more terrain.

Even though it cost me more money than I care to admit, I'm glad I invested. (It's become even more prohibitively expensive now!) It rarely leaves its box for now, but it will... one day it will...

--

Immensely satisfying. I spent two hours yesterday building a scenario with almost all my bits (super fun in itself), then another two hours just now playing an epic 2v2 game on it. The game was impressively dynamic, with the apparent advantage swinging back and forth several times, and the tension remaining high throughout. I'm upping my rating for this game.

--

I'm on a pattern of getting this out about annually, and it's always a hoot. Although, last time I got trounced because we played with the base set (plus a bunch of extra terrain) and I let my new-to-the-game opponent draft his entire army first. No way I can beat an army including Raelin, Syvarris, the paratroopers AND the marro warriors. I was left with vikings and shit.

RATING: 8
I'm not typically fond of toy-like games. But when Toys-R-Us was running their 2-for-1 sales on Hasbro games late in 2004, I picked up a couple copies, figuring that they were a good deal at $20 apiece and wouldn't be hard to unload if necessary. For months, those ugly, hulking boxes just sat on the shelf, exiled to my back room, and I was vaguely ashamed of owning them. 

Once I finally tried the darn game, I was a bit surprised to discover that it was actually a lot of fun! I've since collected almost all of the assorted junk that Hasbro has pushed my way, and despite occasionally suffering some buyer's remorse, I am still enjoying Heroscape.  I always appreciate games that are great fun for mixed groups of kids and adults. There are far too few of those games, and Heroscape is tough to beat in this category. It's not something I'd choose to play in my gaming group (for starters, it simply takes too long to construct and put away), but I'm very happy to have it around.

RATING: 2

The game itself can be pricey.  

Components are very nice with the figures actually being better than expected.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
After three plays.  I'm not a minis-wargame fan in any way, shape or form.  Having said that, I love HeroScape.  It's clearly targeting mainstream/younger crowds, but there's enough of a game for folks like me who have no time for Mage Knight, Warhammer, etc.  

The mechanics - movement, damage, combat, flying, unique characters as well as "squads" of three or four, special attacks that break the rules - are nuanced, deep, and steamlined enough to avoid the minute fiddly details that normally drive me away from meatier minis table-top gaming.  

I especially like the turn order mechanism: players are use four turn tokens numbered 1,2,3, and X.  Players place turn tokens on any characters/army cards they wish to move, and then will each move their 1's, 2's, and 3's after rolling for initiative.  The X is a bluff token each turn.  So when planning, one can consider who potentially will be moving on the other team, although when they will move that turn is unknown.  

This game gets you playing, and has lots of tension and tactics and replay.  For a MB game you get enormous value for your dollar - 30 detailed painted figures, and an innovative interlocking terrain system to design battlefields.  

My only gripe is that the box will barely hold the entire game (and will cease to if I buy expansions). Also a caution that the battlefield terrain setup each game takes at least 20 minutes minimum, so keep that in mind if you're playing with younger players. 

Great gateway to tabletop stuff, and the hobby surrounding it (painting, minis, etc).  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Awsome game, extremely useful for attracting new gamers to miniature games due to flexibility and easy learning curve but still fun to play over and over

RATING: N/A
Originally rated a 9, but the more I play the more I love it. Rapidly becoming my favorite game of all time. Only possible drawback is setup time, but I can make a quick map off the top of my head in only a couple minutes. And the setup time is a necessary evil for the flexibility allowed in the system. Easy to teach to everyone, and everyone I have taught has enjoyed it. Lots of dice rolling, yet the real strategy comes from army synergy and clever piece movement. Every time I read a comment about the luck in this game it makes me want to challenge the person to a game with one of the big tournament winners and explain why they lose 9 times out of 10. Infinitely replayable, truly never the same game twice. The permutations of maps and armies are uncountable. If you have to play only one game for the rest of your life, that game should be Heroscape.

RATING: N/A
The greatest game of all time. I have my oldest son to thank for exposing me to it and starting my interest proper in board games. Looking through the TRU catalog, choosing something for Santa to bring him for Christmas, 2004, he stated, " I want this." I took a look at the image and description for Heroscape and replied, "So do [i]I![/i]"

Six days after receiving the master set, on New Years Day, 2005, my son's fifth birthday, he received a complete set of Mallidon's Prophecy. 

The rest is pure miniatures n' terrain building history, coupled with the best online fan community through three websites. Long live Heroscape.

Favorite Wave: Jandar's Oath for the variety of commons squads

Top 10 units in no particular order. but note I always enjoyed the high-movement units:
Cyprien Esenwein
Sir Dupuis
Isamu
Aubrien Archers
Marrden Hounds
Sujoah

Zombies of Morindan
Shades of Bleakewoode
Me-Burq-Sa

Least favorite:
Major Q9
Deathreavers
Dund
Those elven Wizards, but Morsbane was always pretty cool

RATING: 9
Initial ranking after a few first games (8).  My sons loved it.  I think the rating will go up with more plays.  Great theme, no downtime, simple rules, a fair amount of luck to make the game slightly unpredictable and lots of FUN. 

One more note.  The customization aspect of this game is awesome.  If you have other miniatures, it is very easy to write your own army cards and invent custom rules.  

One of the advantages of Heroscape is that, you can customize it to fit your needs.  By capping the army limit, you control the game length.  By building your own map and choosing one of many scenarios, you make each game different.  

The possibilities are overwhelming considering such simple rules.

An important note.  This game is ADDICTIVE. If you like it, you will soon want to have all the expansions and figures.  Multiple sets are required to build impressive maps, otherwise you will feel a little disappointed by comparing your designs with the photos on Heroscapers. I am not yet at this point, as this hits your pocket hard, but I think that I will try to complete the collection and have at least one unit of each available.

With +70 games played, I have upgraded the ranking to 10, because the game deserves it.  In contrast to many eurogames, each game tells a story and you can actually remember battles even after several weeks.    

Remember: buy at least TWO from each COMMON SQUAD expansion pack.  Certain units simply play better when you have more figures and it is easier to control your army when you have fewer army cards on your side.

-1 for setup time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is an awesome game, its simple to learn and teach. It has a simple yet fun mechanic, creating your team through the point based system is great and decently balanced, consider this the poor man's table top game (the likes of Warhammer and Iron Kingdom). Building your stage can also be as fun as playing on it, because being able to have custom maps is one of the best features of this game. Unlike most board games, this one has expansions similiar to (TCG) trading card games, adding to the already huge pool of characters to play from every year. Another great feature is the marker system, it is a very creative way of taking turns and actions, as you can set a simple unit to act multiple times, or spread them out, there is also a decoy marker which adds to the deception. Overall a great game to have.

RATING: 8.4
Mi juego ideal de escaramuzas: sencillo, con poderes variables, escalable y ¡con metajuego! Para personas sin tiempo para pintar o aprender tochos de reglas. Satisface mis expectativas de jugón (suficientes posibilidades estratégicas), de padre (disfruto jugándolo con mis hijos) y del niño que llevo dentro (¿a quién no le gusta un juego con samurais, ninjas, vaqueros, robots, zombies, elfos, dragones, aliens, comandos...?) Más táctico de lo que parece (por los glifos, la altura, el terreno y la construcción del ejército). Buenísima mecánica la de la línea de visión (sin dudas en un 99% de las ocasiones) PROS: Los héroes parecen héroes (son más fuertes). Poderes especiales chulísimos (hacen distintos cada ejército gracias a sus sinergias). Terreno en 3D. Más barato que otros juegos de miniaturas. CONS: Hay dados y suerte. Si el terreno es grande, se dedica mucho tiempo en el setup. Tortura para completistas. Descatalogado.

Reglas caseras que podrían usarse:

Cambiar tirar 2 dados de ataque por una calavera; 3 dados de defensa por un escudo; 6 dados de valkiria por un éxito con el estarndarte.

Probar a eliminar el bonificador de altura superior en el ataque a distancia

Subo su nota de 7.5 a 8.2 tras mi primera partida con mis hijos.

RATING: 10
The master set comes with everything you need to get started. Lots of figures, terrain and even some ruins. The figures come painted already as well so you don't have to mess around with that nonsense either.

There are tons of expansions to buy and can give you a ton of options when deciding what army you want to play. In addition there are special terrain expansions as well to help reduce the effectiveness of range. (Jungle, Glaciers, Road/Forest).

There is a luck element however most games are won by smart tactical decisions and careful order marker placement rather then lucky die rolls. To prove this point even further the same player has won both Indy GenCon Championships for 2006/2008. I myself have won both the 2007/2009 GenCon Championships. Are we just lucky or good? I'd say a little bit of both. It just really hammers down the point though that more often then not the player that is a better tactician has the advantage. 

I rated this a 10 simply for the significant impact this game has had on me. It was a huge gateway game into board gaming for me. In addition I have loved the many different ways I have played this game. The tournament scene, huge team battles, or simply big free for all battles are all a lot of fun. This game has gotten the most replay value out of all games I currently own and I can see myself playing this 5-10 years down the road.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

2011-10-15 

Initial Rating: 8.5 (September 2010)

I love miniatures and this game has tons and tons of them. Sadly I have played it only once, but it was great.

The components are the main factor here, they are absolutely stunning, the miniatures very detailed, the terrain very well done and you can create any map you want adding to the replayability factor.

This is a fairly shallow tactical game although I confess we played with the basic rules. It has a reasonable amount of luck (but you can mitigate that playing with the probabilities). The game is great for children and the fun factor is through the roof.

My only dislike is having to pack all the bits again after a play, it is a pain.

Love to see there are a lot of expansions.

This game was once in my top 10 list of favorite games.

Current Rating: 8.5

2017-02-20

It’s been years since I last played Heroscape Master Set: Rise of the Valkyrie and my gaming tastes have changed a lot these years. I no longer enjoy most Ameritrash games, I´m decidedly an Euro player now so my desire to play again Heroscape is rather low. 

Also, I no longer associate great miniatures with great games. CMON cured me of that malady.

I HATE to build the world in which we are going to fight, sometimes, it takes more than the playing part. The teardown is also a pain.

You don´t need much brain power to play it, that is, is it a game light on meaningful decisions. Perhaps with the expansions it gets better.

I got rid of my copy and I don’t think I will ever play Heroscape again, but I concede it is a great game for children.

RATING: 7
I admit to being torn on how to score this one. The game mechanics are pedestrian, for the most part, but the way the whole package is produced and put together is remarkable. Stealing from Duel of Ages to pit multiple periods and genres against each other is excellent. The terrain tiles, how they are constructed and conceived and are ever-expandable, clearly deserves a "10" rating. Ultimately, I think while combat is lacking enough to keep this from being perfect, but the game is JUST ABOUT perfect for its target audience. This game will be remembered and sought out for a VERY long time. It's a landmark of production, in a way. I'm not the target, but my son is. I can attest that this game meets the designers' goals and then some.

RATING: 5
Heroscape has actually taken a pretty precipitous drop rating-wise since I originally played it.  Early on I would have given it perhaps a 9, based on balance, quality of pieces, ease of play.  However, several factors have conspired to drop it to a 6:

1. In a strange sort of catch-22, the more pieces that become available for this game, the more time-consuming and complicated it gets.  What patience and novelty won early on in terms of map setup and drafting (easily consuming half an hour before you can even begin play) is now pretty much gone.  I can barely even stand to think of playing this anymore as a result.  

2. My patience for games heavily to completely dependent on dice rolls has waned significantly.  

In other words, after spending hours and hours just drafting and building maps alone, Heroscape has moved from a game I used to be semi-fanatical about to a game I'm so unenthused about that all my stuff takes up the same spot on my shelf that it did almost a year ago now. 

4-14-06:  Played a couple games of this over last weekend.  One of them was a 3 on 1, with me the lone defender, adn we had a great game going until the attackers (all three) had a stretch of completely amazing dice rolls (19 out of 20 skulls over a number of rolls) and this completely gutted me.  My dislike for dice mechanics is growing exponentially, so I'm dropping this to a 5.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Have 2x of RotV

Heroscape is the acme of plasticrack. While others have been content merely to create collectible or semi-collectible figures, Heroscape decided to up the ante by throwing in sets of attractive, highly customizable plastic terrain for the figures (and your imagination) to play on. Of course, neither of those things would mean much without solid gameplay, which Heroscape has. A minimalist but thoroughly adequate and satisfying rules system, a nearly endless set of possible map and army combinations, and an enthusiastically supportive community help round out the "package." The only major cons, really, are the relative scarcity of some of the sets (a problem that no doubt will become harder as still more new ones are produced) and the fairly high cost point if you're like me (and I know you are) and have that completist itch. I suppose you could also complain about the longish setup time, but that can be mediated by choosing smaller maps (which often times are just as satisfying as the huge ones).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.4
Number of players: 2-4 (+)

Components: (10)
Isn't that what everyone always thinks of? These crazy terrains. All those painted miniatures?
  
Rules: (10)
The system this game runs on is very simple and easy to grasp. The rule book included an even simpler rule-set, if I recall correctly. There was never any reason to implement that. 

Setup: (1)
:'( I hate setting this game up. I mean, I LOVE having the game set up, I love all that can be done, but I hate actually having to do it.

Area required to play: (1)
This game is going to take up a lot of space. Usually we, and I find many others, play it on the floor.
 
Fun: (10)
This is one of the very most fun games I have ever played! This thing is/was/will always be one of the best things in the world of board gaming.

Theme Integration / Mechanics: (10)
The theme of this thing spilled out of boxes and left puddles in the aisles of Wal-Mart. That's the reason the game was cancelled; big box stores kept suing the company that manufactured it. The mechanics also work well to keep the game moving very quickly while making each unit feel and play differently.

Replay Value: (10)
This game is as re-playable as Magic. With all the different units that were available, and all the customization that a person could add to the game should they so desire, I can't see that I'll ever become board of this game.

Storage: (1)
There's nothing to do except to get some BIG boxes and throw everything you have inside.

Accessibility: (10)
The game really is easy enough to teach to children and the components (especially those minis) make it very appealing to most audiences.

Over-All/Bonuses/Biases:(+10) I really, really love this game. Yes, it's crazy expensive now that it's out of print. Yes, it takes up way too much room. Yes, it's a bastard to set up and take down. I wouldn't actually suggest anyone buy into this game because of the cost, but I do hope (and hope that you hope) that it'll someday come back in to print. Also, if you ever find that you have the chance to play it? PLAY IT!

RATING: 10
I am very hooked on this game...

The basic mechanics are simple and straightforward, making it basically a simple and light miniature wargame, without the many hazzles of "true" tabletop games! The only thing that can´t be counted or meassured is LOS, which should be fairly obvious 99% of the time anyways... The many different squads and heroes, with their myriad special powers makes for endless combinations. Trying to build the perfect army to beat your opponent, and take advantage of the map is fun in itself. The miniatures are very cool and over time some of them really grow on you, and take on a life of their own!

UPDATE: A few years on, I have to admit that I just LOVE Heroscape and everything about it! One of my absolute favourite games. And I have a complete collection! Funny thing is that when it came out, I wrote it off as a childrens game, and only bought it, when I found it cheap on sale, with the intent of using it at the after school club for kids where I work... Things kind of took off after that! I now have a complete collection, complete being at least one of everything ever made for Heroscape, several of some. 
I am the founder, and proud member of [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/347216] the League of Extraordinary Heroscapers[/url], a BGG society for middleaged, and older, men (and 2 women) who still get all giddy playing war with their toy soldiers!

UPDATE: 5 years in, and I still absolutely love Heroscape! Original, Super Heroes or the D&D stuff, it´s all good!

4 sets + most of the terrain from a 5th set

RATING: 7.5
A surprisingly good game about anachronistic monster bashing. I was expecting nothing more than a simple roll-and-hit game, but there's quite a bit of planning and strategy to be had (advanced rules with glyphs).

Components were amazing (modular board makes for amazing scenarios) and fairly well-painted minis. I would've liked some terrain rules (all terrains are the same), but overall, the set is extremely good value for money.

A fun middle-weight game that can be scaled to a player's taste.

RATING: 8
Lots of toys, and I love pre-painted miniatures.  The rules are simple enough to rope interested folks in easily, but leave enough room to create strategies (albeit light ones).  Obviously designed for the pre-teen audience, but is designed very well (a good game, is a good game). This is definitely the best of the Master Sets as it captures the battle across time very well with the variety of armies it comes with.

RATING: 8.7
I have had this game for one year now and I thouroughly enjoy it.  It has the random factor of rolling the dice, but I enjoy that in a game.  In my mind Heroscape is what Battle Chess should have been.  You have a given movement for each character.  Line of sight and relative elevation make a difference.  I also love all of the special abilities of all of the characters.  Between the large variety of characters and the modular board I have never played a game that was the same.  

One of the few things I didn't like was the way the turns are organized for the rounds.  The way it is set up Grimak could take three turns in a row while your samuri sit back and pick their nose.  I altered this rule so in each round every character gets one turn.  This has enabled epic battles with very large armies.  It also aliviates the problem of on person picking a couple of very expensive characters and another person picking a several less expensive characters and not being able to gang up on the larger more expensive characters.  

All in all its a great game that is simple enough for 10 year old to grasp but complex enough to keep an adult interested.

One last thing I really have enjoyed is seeing all of the creative custom characters people have made.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
What I like:
- Some games can be epic (like a 4-player scenario that was so balanced that it all came down to a few, climatic dice rolls).
- Many scenarios, with many different flavors.
- Nice special powers.  The various cards really have a different feel.
- The fact that special powers are on cards makes them more "real" than the powers printed in tiny icons on the base of LotR: Combat Hex minis.
- Heroes really feel like heroes: their strong.
- Faster combats than in LotR: Combat Hex (fewer dice).
- Nice miniatures, with various sizes: nice variety.
- Simple and fluid system, with interesting tactical possibilities.
- Interesting tactical choices, thanks to the card ordering system; the stacking of markers is also interesting.
- The 3D terrain is much richer in tactical terms than a map.  The visual and tactile aspect of various heights is a plus.
- The visual aspect allows one to really see a kind of movie unfold; this "story" aspect makes games more memorable.
- Nice support (FAQ).
- How to play well is not so obvious: the army must be chosen well, the threats correctly assessed, and it is not so easy to find enough time to think about a sound strategy with some many actions taking place everywhere on the board (which tend to bring the focus to tactical issues).

What I do not care for:
- A little long, for the depth (compare Race for the Galaxy!) or the tenseness (compare Space Hulk).
- Setup a little long (10'?).
- More chaotic than Lotr: Combat Hex, because a single mini can move three times in a single turn, and because you plan 3 actions without knowing what your opponent will do.
- The terrain does not look really good.

Overall conclusion:
- Better miniature game than LotR: Combat Hex, except for the setup time.  More flavor (creature cards, visual appeal, varied figures), fewer dice, more tactical possibilities (3D terrain, ordering of orders).
- Not as tense as Space Hulk, which is currently my favorite miniatures game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
A light tactical miniature game.  The minis are painted and have a wide group of "armies" ranging from Viking heros to a guy on a T-Rex.  You organize your tools on plastic terrain and fight it out against you opponent.  Each army has a special ability and it is fun quick game.  

Setup of the plastic pieces on the map can take a while.

The one big hit against this game is the that the plastic water tiles are extremely fragile and are easily broken.  

A solid game though especially good for kids.

RATING: 7
The outstanding modular terrain is really the star (especially for game designers or those who want nicer maps for their OTHER board games), but the minis, accessories, and all are very nice. It's still worth tracking this game down.

ADDENDUM: Months later, this remains one of my favorite games for 1v1, 2v1, and 1v1v1. It has both heavy and eclectic themes which play out in the units' abilities and behaviors. The base rules aren't the best, but even playing by those, HeroScape is great fun. Now that its popularity has lulled, it's easy to get your hands on lots of its material.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I played this with my nephew, and it was merely okay. I'm not sure we were playing by the rules, since I never actually saw them, and many things seemed to go in a manner quite convenient for him. It didn't help much when I kept rolling nine dice and getting zero shields--I believe it happened three times. Yikes. It still was a close game, although I lost in the end.

Nice bits, simple combat system, seems to work all right. Maybe not deep enough for my tastes. This is one of those games that, given the motivation and time, I would completely rewrite to suit my desire for a more complicated, realistic tactical system. Then again, it features heroes with lasers and mofo guns fighting samurai and orcs, so realism isn't something this game cares much about. There's a reason armies gave up fighting with swords after guns were perfected. But taken for what it is, this might be a fun game with the right opponent, and the bits certainly are lovely. Why do the primitive types have ranged weapons that can shoot as far as the modern and futuristic types with guns and blasters and whatnot? This bothers me a great deal, but it does not seem to bother too many others. If you demand internal consistency in a game, this is not for you.

This is the board game equivalent of Angelina Jolie--a beautiful, sexy mess. I know it's flawed, but I stare longingly at it and dream of fondling the bits.

  After watching a bunch of kids playing this game at the library, and after purchasing the Marvel set and some more terrain/expansion packs, I'm thinking that maybe this should be a 6 instead of a 5. It's so easy to get into, and the scale issues with primitive versus futuristic ranged weapons can be solved so easily by not mixing those types, that maybe I was unfair in docking it a point for that.

Update: Okay, fine, it's a 6. Are you happy? Fine, it's a 7. Now are you finally happy? I certainly hope so, because that's absolutely, positively, the highest I can go.

I'm a bit amused by the Heroscape Weenies who are obsessive about using the "best" units and combos. I don't give a rat's you-know-what if cybernetic gorillas and fire elementals work well together. I just want to push my monkeys around and then set stuff on fire, okay? So get off my back about that.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The best miniatures skirmish game I've ever played.
This Master Set combines heroes and creatures from very different backgrounds, which is one of its attractives for me but may feel weird for new players.

PROS
- Amazing terrain: absolutely no other game looks this good when displayed on the table.
- Good-looking pre-painted figures.
- Easy to teach and learn.
- Simple atributes and powers system for the characters, with no complicated rules nor exceptions.
- Simple movement and combat system: no need for rulers nor any other components.
- High level of strategy with the possibility of bluffing and deceiving.
- The possibility of creating an unlimited number of scenarios and variants.

CONS
- The almost inexistent distribution in Spain.
- The fact that it has been discontinued for a lot of years, so finding material isn't easy nor cheap.

Another plus to this collectable game is that the expansion packs are NOT blind so you know exactly what you're getting in each blister pack.

Very customizable and fun. The only downside is the preparation (which could take up to half an hour) and the clean up.

RATING: 6.5
3 copies.

A very good game with more strategy and tactics than many give it credit for. The game is interesting in the initial stages as you need to draft your army while taking into account the terrain of each scenario as well as beneficial and often symbiotic special powers of your various figures.
Game play itself is interesting as there is a nice balance between tactics,strategy and luck...one of the better mixes in any game I've played actually.

Replayability is enhanced by the many creative scenarios posted online as well as the ability to design your own maps and scenarios with the various terrain options. HS has a LOT going for it... plays well with 2-8+ players, is very different from one game to the next, encourages creativity in the scenario creation as well as the actual game play and as a bonus is a great family game to play with the kids. Downgraded to a 6.5 recently as the "spark" for this game has left me somewhat. Although this is the most played game in our collection...the need to keep things fresh with new expansions  can make the game a bit of a money pit.

RATING: 9
At first I thought heroscape was a simplified miniatures game with cool minis and awesome terrain.  But as I have explored this game, I've really come to appreciate the incredible strategic depth it offers.  The toys are still awesome, but it is the mechanics that make this game shine.  Secretly issuing orders at the start of a turn adds an incredible amount of strategy.  And the rest of the rules strip away the frustrating parts of miniatures combat, allowing you to focus on the battle and not on the rules.  Add to that infinitely customizable scenarios, cool draft and constructed play, and room for literally any number of players, and this game is a 9, pure and simple.  Given enough time to play, I cannot imagine I would ever turn down a game of Heroscape.

RATING: 8
x2

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The Background

I have become a late convert to Heroscape. Having walked past it on the shelves of various stores in Scotland, I saw an article on BGG stating it was for sale in Argos UK for the unbelievable price of £7.99, so naturally I succumbed and bought two.

I have two young sons aged six and ten and I am a kick in the backside off my sixtieth birthday. The three of us enjoy playing BattleLore, Memoir '44, Battle Cry and Descent. The kids certainly love the role playing aspects of Descent and have taken it to heart. Since playing Heroscape, Descent has not touched the table.

The Contents

So, why all the excitement? First of all you get a massive amount of plastic terrain; a veritable "Lego" set of hexagonal tiles with which you can create an endless assortment of three dimensional battlefields. These come in three colours: green representing grass, blue-grey representing rock and sand representing, well, sand. Bright blue water hexes are also included.

Then there are the figures. Thirty in the base set. These comprise heroes and squads and range from WWII airborne through robots and Vikings to dragons. Now this is a pretty eclectic mix but the gameplay allows you to bring them all together and after a while, you don't even think about matching up a secret agent with a winged warrior. The sheer look of joy on the kid's faces when they saw the variety and quality of the figures had to be seen to be believed.

The Gameplay

Now, my two little offspring fall into the demonic rather than the angelic category. They love gory movies and generally anything that has a bit of good old-fashioned slaughter and skulduggery in it. Heroscape is ideal for getting them battling across a table with miniatures rather than tearing lumps out of each other.

Each squad or hero comes with a card detailing statistics; how far they move, the range of their attack, their ability in defence and attack and how many hits they take before they croak. There is also a points cost which allows an army to be drafted. Two sets of rules are included: a (very) basic and a "master" set. Both the kids were into the master set straight away as it allows them to use each unit's special powers.

They and I took to it like a duck to water. I heartily recommend purchasing two sets if you have two kids. This avoids real bloodshed when they are drafting their armies and both want the same hero.

The Road to Perdition

Heroscape should carry a government health warning as it is totally addictive and has lead me to purchase several expansions. Trees, bridges, castles, glaciers and lava fields along with a multitude of extra troops will tempt you and melt the plastic straight through your wallet.

Naming and Shaming

We have ended up giving our own names to several of the characters and this reinforces the role-playing element. The agents below are Sean Connery, Morgan Freeman and Diana Rigg (Remember her from the Avengers anyone?). It can of course backfire. My ten-year-old was overheard calling Raelin "Twinkle-tits." I even have my own favourite - Maximus Phallus and the Ninth Legion - the kids don't speak Latin yet.

I rate this game a seven. That is my subjective judgement based solely on the great time I have playing it with my boys. It is not for everyone. I also play serious wargames and Heroscape is a delightfully different kettle of fish.

RATING: 10
My favourite game of all time !!

Most fun game of all. The customization of your army and the tactical aspect of this game is endless. 

The peoples who dislikes this game have no idea how deep this game can be. All the depth comes from how you build you entire army and how will you use it against your opponents.

Sure there is luck factor with the dice mechanic, but it can be reduced by planning and optimizing your movements. The best players are usually the ones who considers their statistical probabilities and gauge their decisions accordingly.

I can guarantee that not a single new player would be able to beat me in his first 20 games at least, as characters knowledge and playing/knowing the match-ups are important parts of this game.

This game has it all, the artwork of the cards, the modular maps are amazing and the miniatures are cool and top notch quality. Creating the map is almost as fun as playing the game. 10/10 for components.

This game can be played free for all, 4 way battle royal, team matches, but the competitive gameplay is the head to head battle. One vs One is where this game shines and the main reason the tournament scene kept this game alive until today and probably for years to come. People are so passionate about this game that it exists hundreds of fan made character creations. Just to give you an idea how this game became a cult over the years.

We played hundreds of times with families, friends, neighbours... Won numerous organized tournaments against other top players. I've done it all.

I would recommend it to everyone. Best game of all time easily !! It's now a classic as I don't believe another game with the same quality as Heroscape will see the day.

Heroscape.....How I love thee

RATING: 6
Originally I was not impressed with the game play found in Heroscape. Yeah the eye candy was there but where was the depth. Having played 'deeper' miniature games and many games of Mage Knight (as well as the other 'clix' games) I had to re-evaluate my thoughts on this game. 

What caused me to re-think Heroscape was the fun factor. In every other mini's game, there is always some struggle with the rules (or the damned rulers); at times this sucked the fun out of the game. I can say that I have never played a game of Heroscape when this occurred; I have never played a game that wasn't fun. 

It requires little effort to introduce new players, set up balanced armies, etc. Complexity is not equivalent to 'good'. Heroscape is 'good'. It does what it expected and does it well.

Though it had taken awhile before I recognized the excellence of this design but I finally saw it. 

This is a great game.


Note: I have little more than the original base set and it has served me well.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The figures are beautiful and the terrain is like minecraft made physical. I love building the maps and then designing the armies. Games go quickly, and the limitation of only allowing three groups to activate per round is really nice. It puts this powerful power limiter that makes something this scale manageable.

I also love the sanity rules of 'if the mini can see the other mini it has line of sight' and the 'if the guy can't fit in that space, he can't go through that underpass'.

It does use dice for combat, so the best laid plans can be foiled by a bad roll, but that comes with the territory sometimes.

There are tons of figures and expansions available for this game. For the most part it's balanced, using the points system to purchase army cards before the start of the game. That being said, it's not 100%. Make agreements with players before selecting armies about what sort of armies are going to fight. Don't pair an army of elves vs the Incredible Hulk.

:star: Art, Iconography and components functional
:nostar: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:star: Multiple plays stay interesting
:nostar: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::star::star: Raw enjoyment

RATING: 10
Probably the best boardgame for me with Star Wars Epic Duels Game. More a toy than a game, lot of luck involved and some tactic, but... what a FUN blast! Really, really fun, with fantastic components (...but terrible box, at least for the first base set!)
This game is simply awesome: a real system, simple, modular and with high custom possibilities for a literally endless experience. I play on large maps adding a very light quest system and an area-control mechanic, both generating Victory Points as a win condition; the game is more intriguing now, not completely focused on random skirmishes, while the additional mechanics incentivize a better map exploration. Also, the quest aspect adds an exciting adventure feeling.
My rate of 10 is for the entire Heroscape saga, not only the Rise of the Valkyrie set.

I have 5 starter sets, 2 Marro starters (with some more spare parts), 3 Forgotten Forest, 3 Tundra (with some more spare parts), 2 Jungle, 2 Fortress, 2 Volcarren and all the expansions and promos, plus a bunch of doubles (all common squads 3x/4x/5x), over 100 custom figures (Mage Knight, World of Warcraft, Horrorclix and D&D Miniatures, all re-based) and some custom terrains.
I have also the Marvel set but I don't like it very much and I use it generally on its own (and very rarely).

I bought Battle for the Underdark (2 sets) and the 3 D&D Waves (all 3x/4x), but I don't like the miniature recycling Wizards of the Coast did with the game; despite some good interactions and mechanics, D&D Miniatures are clearly different in quality, colours (some are also really bad painted) and out of size. For me the 'real' Heroscape ends with Wave 10.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The best miniatures game out there for light wargaming with a fantasy, kid-like feel to have FUN with. After reading about and playing hundreds of different games, I still come back to Heroscape as hitting the right sweet spot between casual and competetive miniatures play. The pre-painted figures and 3D hex terrain makes it very appealing and easy to enter into a light miniatures game. The hodge-podge of themes, time-eras, dinosaurs, army men, aliens, historical, and creatures is a dream for light-hearted players who always wanted to battle them together. Literally, this is the game I waited my whole life for. It's the perfect blend of chunk and kid-like appeal for imaginative fun for all ages and genders. And with the deals that have been available ($20 for the entire RotV Master Set?), it is a no-brainer to pick up if there are players it would remotely appeal to.
Biggest drawback is how the dice regularly make a mockery of turn order, positioning, unit choice, and any other strategy. 
Best house rules (if less randomness is desired, or if ranged units are overly dominating) are:
1) Allow players to change in (before rolling) 2 attack dice for 1 skull, 3 defense dice for 1 shield, and 6 Valkyrie dice for a Valk symbol.
and
2) Eliminate the elevation bonus for ranged attacks. There's zero thematic justification for benefiting elevated ranged attacks, and lots of in-game reasoning to not provide it (makes ranged too dominant).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.7
[b][color=#CC0000] 

Essentially a perfect game.  I'm not just talking gameplay -- I'm talking the entire execution of the product.  This is a game designed to appeal to ages 3 through 100, has magnificent components that are designed to be brutalized by small children with little or no damage resulting, and to appeal to all on three levels -- building, role-playing, and competing.  Nothing in the marketplace is at the same level as Heroscape from an overall packaging perspective.

Available for $18US for a period of time, I simply don't think any other game has ever provided this level of value at this price point.  Or even close.  None ever will again, because the nature of the World's economy has fundamentally changed.  The door has closed on this level of material for that kind of price.

Fun game.  Great for boys between five and ninety-five.  I've played the advanced rules with my five-year-old twins.  A bit of patience was required, but they had fun.  The big pieces make for an impressive look and feel which is not lost on kids.  Many expansions -- you [i]could[/i] drop a few buckazoids on this critter, but you don't [i]have[/i] to.  Requires a bit of time and space to set it up, but once it's there it is positively glorious.  The quality of the components is simply magnificent -- gorgeous AND tough.  

My kids love all aspects of it -- playing pretend, setting up the boards like a puzzle, playing.  This is THE game for young boys of this generation to own.  This is the one they'll talk about with each other on the golf course fifty years from now.

This basic set is the one to go for -- nice variety of pieces and plenty to play with -- you need never buy an expansion.  Simple rules means thirty minutes to master the concepts, then you can play for hours.  Short quick battles, huge drawn-out campaigns . . . anything is possible given the modularity and variability of the pieces and their basic concepts.  

Simply the best birthday present you'll ever give a seven-year-old boy.  If you see this grab two copies -- you'll likely have grandsons someday.

RATING: 8
This is a rating for the Heroscape system as a whole, rather than this specific set.

A moment of silence for Heroscape, the game that tried to make minis games as accessible and straightforward as they possible could be. That it succeeded so wildly is admirable, and over a decade removed Heroscape still is an impressive game. The physical production is unmatched, and will likely remain so. It's incredibly easy to just throw together a board and bash out a 45 minute scenario, but you can also throw things together and create something genuinely epic. It's a really fun game, and I wish it could have gone on for longer.

RATING: 9
Fantastic game.

I was dubious at first, but followed the advice of many on the Geek. The theme, whilst slightly childish, is also quite amazing and gives scope which is practically unequalled. 

The game-play has a simplicity which makes even the so-called 'advanced game' far simpler than most in my collection, but has enough tactics and options to keep you going back again and again. The luck-element is important, but can easily be offset by proper army construction and other things. Whilst I've played 'deeper' games, and I've played games which are 'better' with more innovation or thought behind them, you'd be hard-pressed to find a 'funner' game.

This base-set alone has enough terrain to make dozens of different set-ups, with elevation, rivers, caves, and ruins all being possible in many combinations. Coupled with other packs, this provides a game with huge re-playability and fun.

RATING: 9
I bought 1 Master Set but several multiples of most Boosters and a ton of terrain tiles on e-bay. I like playing themed armies, Romans versus Orcs or Marro or something.

The terrain is adaptable to A&A minis and other games. 

The real "strategy" is drafting an appropriate force for the battlefield. The more expansions one has, and in many cases that means duplicates and triplicates of boosters, the more strategies one can implement.  

Tactically HS is not exactly a brain
burner but the combination of melee, ranged and flying units does allow tactical players to establish kill zones of combined arms so to speak. Actually it is a better tactical game than M'44. 

But I don't get to play it often at all. Ya see, two of my gamer friends either don't drive or don't have a car. I'd like to leave it set it up here  and have folks over to play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
This is an important step "back" for commercial boardgames, in so many ways. Just imagine if Heroscape were designed as a collectible game -- it would only have, at max, a 9 month life-span!

Just deviating from the collectible market allows the game to return to proper strategy game roots, (not the common, uncommon, rare hierarchy) and it's there in the drafting, the troop movement/engagement rules, the height advantage, and the glyphs. The rules form an interesting skein. All of these things together and the open-ness make this the "Unreal Tournament of Board Games", and that also means an endless stream of fun mods for years to come.

Hasbro has been experimenting with low-run, high quality toys in the past years since Pokemon (Xevoz for instance), so it would be nice to see them apply that niche-friendly model to this game for another year and a half at least.
