RATING: 8.3
I would not normally have thought I would ever like a game like this one, but I got it as a gift...and loved it.  Imagine a 10 year old taking their mixed up toybox of random plastic soldiers from all eras, plastic space explorers, little dinosaurs, fast-food restaurant toys, ponies, gremlins, unicorns, plus every imaginable 1/6 scale action figure...and somehow making a light tactical wargame out of it!...which is more or less what highly imaginative children do when they throw all these things together and create little towns, villages and battles from an enormously disparate collection of unrelated toys.  Add in Legos, Megablocks, Lincoln Logs and Tinker Toys as terrain, and Voila(!)...you've got HeroScape!!  Not to be taken too seriously, but really fun (surprisingly so).  Unfortunately I could never get any of my "serious" wargamer friends to play, and after playing only three times in my life, all of which were with my 11 year old youngest daughter...I had to sell it all off.

RATING: 9
(x8)

For those like me who are dying to get into miniatures wargaming, but do not have the time to paint and assemble figures and terrain, Heroscape scratches the itch quite well.  However, as a base game, the rules are a little too simple.  But it seems that they were intentionally left open-ended so that each owner could customize the rules to the complexity they want.  So, with a little house-ruling, this can be the game you want, at a fraction of the cost of something like Warhammer.

It is certainly worth the little extra effort.  Not to say that even the base rules are no fun--they are fun indeed.  I was really surprised by this game.

RATING: 7
HeroScape. Many argue, "It's a toy more than a game!" Others reply, "It's a game more than a toy!"

Relax. It's both, and it's quite engaging. The ability to battle it out between heroes from across all space and time on an infinite variety of battlefields, where the victory conditions are limited only by one's imagination, is a lot of fun.

The units are varied and interesting. Building and designing new battlefields keeps things exciting, and the game can be easily played with 2-4 players. It is also fairly accessible to younger players.

The luck factor is there (although it seems higher than it actually is), and that can be a turn-off for some people, but it also induces nail-biting tension. The tension is great, but it would be nice to have some rule variants that diminish the luck a little bit, as it can seem overwhelming at time. (Update: playing the Master game with the Basic game's turn structure balances the game more to my liking - it increases the ability of a player to pursue an effective strategy and diminishes the chance of rolling for initiative, and makes the game more fun to play - and faster to boot. But for those considering playing with this rule alteration, I recommend playing the Master game as is first.)

I can't think of any other game that's as fun to both play and play WITH! It's also expandable! The game is fairly light, but the simplicity of adding house rules can make it heavier. I think the first expansion is the best.

CHILDREN'S RATING: 8.5

Am finding this is a fun option for small children - playing with the basic rule set. You can contextualize the characters as doing battle with other as part of a contest of some sort where losers have to sit out to the next game. "Killing" isn't really a necessary aspect of HeroScape. Little ones will also enjoy making up stories with the characters for imaginative play. You should hear my daughter tell her stories about Deathwalker, Mimring, and Raelin. They are hilarious and entertaining. She also really enjoys building the battlefields.

Update: The synergy that can be generated between different sorts of units is like a Magic: TG - "lite". The intricacy of both strategy and tactics increases and the luck factor decreases. Good drafting becomes much more important. With the expansions in play, of course, the game becomes more difficult to win for a child playing against an adult, but things are easily leveled out by giving the child more points with which to draft.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Some call it a kids game, or a game for adults who don't want to grow up.  Maybe it's true.  However, this game is a lot of fun, because you can do so much with it.  Can be kind of expensive when you start adding on expansions, but most of them are definitely worthwhile.

RATING: 6
Pre-painted plastic minis and a very modular playing board make this game very visually appealing for those who do not have the patience or finances for Games Workshop.  Like most head-to-head tabletop war games, most of the time, a game comes down to luck of the dice throws, but I enjoyed drafting an army by points, and responding to the units my opponent had drafted based on each character's stats and special abilities.
Also like many table top war games, the acquisition of additional armies is essential for having a varied experience, but because of the theme, there is no real need to specialize in one army.
I would only recommend this for people that are as interested in shaping the hexagon-based terrain for their battles (like Legos) as they are in the actual combat experience.

RATING: 8

RATING: 7
[many plays] (rating is for the base game   any number of expansions.  Too many expansions for me to keep straight and rate individually). 
Pros: Great looking pieces, easy to learn, non-collectible.  Has a lot of variety to it and good replay value.  It has basic rules making it accessible to kids and advanced rules which give it a little more meat for adults.  
Cons: It just is so basic and non-original.  Each unit has x number of attack dice, y number of defense, z number movement and some special ability.  Each turn you move, you fight, you roll dice.  repeat repeat repeat.  
[update] After playing in an all day 6 round tournament, I concede this game has a lot more strategy then I had previously given it credit for.  It really does lend itself well to a tournament like that.  A Heroscape tournament is a lot of fun, and really I challenge anyone who participated in a good tournament to think that it just comes down to a bunch of dice rolling. Increasing my rating by .5.

RATING: 10
I love this game, its one of my all time favorites.  Overall it blows other miniatures games I've played out of the H20. Simple, but deep miniature war gaming (deep enough for me anyways).  Doesn't take itself too seriously.  Modular 3D terrain makes a huge difference.  Expandable, not collectible.  Some surprisingly nice pre-painted minis.  Great fanbase and support.  Is marred by poor product distribution and is annoyingly marketed to the wrong demographic.  Probably my biggest gripe is with some nefarious marketing tactics that force you to buy multiple expansions to get the most out of other units you've purchased.  It would be a near perfect game if not for this.   Still, this is one of my favorite games, and it has enormous untapped potential as a game system.

RATING: 7
The best prepainted minis game I've seen*. Blows Clix games right out of the water. Has tactics, strategy, and army building, plays right out of the box. The constructable hex terrain is simply awesome. As for the figures... well, some of them are good, with inking and washing that prepaints usually don't have. Some of them kind of suck, but is still better than what else you could get at the same price. I will say it again: for what it is, it is THE BEST. 

Unfortunately the logistics involved in collecting, transporting and fielding so many plastic men keep this from being played more often, but that is a problem of the genre, not of the game. 

* As of 2009. Later on, Monsterpocalypse and X-Wing really showed me how a good minis game could do its thing while still not needing a big footprint. Let me tell you. That Heroscape terrain is pretty, but it is not worth the hassle.

RATING: 10
Simple skirmish battle rules, yet not simplistic. The combination of the elegant order system and combat system, the mix of squads vs heroes, special powers that make the tactical decisions fun & interesting, a variety of soldiers from all time periods which oozes theme, and the inclusion of glyphs to add twists/objectives to the game, all result in a terrific game play experience. 

And for gamers who love "bits", the Rise of the Valkyrie set contains the best components of any game under $75 that I've ever found in my life. Simply astounding value for the money. This is the best of all the HeroScape master sets by far. 

There isn't a better skirmish game in a box. BRILLIANT!

For the purposes of the 'game' it would be just as engaging (which means 'not very') to do away with everything except the dice. It would not change the fundemental way the game plays. The only possible redeeming quality is that it may be a 'gateway' game for current non (or young) gamers who do not yet fully appreciate what a game can really be.

RATING: 9

The sheer amount of terrain provided makes for a pretty varied and expandable game and offers a lot of variety.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I bought my first copy at Essen 2004 for 65 EUR. I bought a second english set for 55 EUR because of the sparkly water and red & blue dice...

This game is very popular with the children I play it with. After the spectacular battle ends, they always want to play "free-format", i.e. building their own landscapes and armies and just use it as a toy.

One of our own scenarios with kids is to make a huge battlefield and dropping 5 treasures on it. They need to be gathered and are each worth a whopping 50 points. As soon as a figure hits the treasure, it is transported back to its starters zone (makes the rules really easy). Treasures include jewels (emerald and ruby) from Astoria, gold and pirate ships (to be placed on water tiles) from Age of Empires III, and of course flags on the castle walls...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
It can be fun, but the game tends to drag on.  And on.  And on.  You usually know who's going to win within forty-five minutes:  a game can last three hours or more with the expansions added.  Round limits are a necessity, and even then, Heroscape falls victim to a "rich get richer" problem.  A few bad rolls early in the game can cost you a few units.  Those few units can cost you access to glyphs, which do things like add one to your attack roll, and so on.  With those, of course, you lose a few more units, and the effects become insurmountable.  I have yet to see an army use superior strategy to overcome a larger force, simply because I don't think it's really possible given the ruleset.

That said, I will generally play, though I'm plagued with a conflict of interest:  my friend, who owns the game, likes to play with huge armies.  I would rather play skirmishes because, in a short game, the flaws of the system don't have time to emerge...

I recommend it for the figurines to use in other games, but I don't recommend the game itself!

RATING: 9.5
A game beyond games.  I can't give it a 10 because it's just too fiddly to pull out frequently.  The plastic pieces for this game are so amazingly detailed, the endless variety of boards so fascinating in their 3D eccentricity, that you just gotta love this game.  Rules are straight-forward and self-apparent and it just has an atmosphere that is enjoyable.  I have a bunch of expansions and a whole crate of pieces, so I'll just say... I would play this any time.  

Only down-side.  Set up takes a while.  Yet, even setup is enjoyable.  With a new person to games, this game should be setup before they even arrive at your house.

RATING: 6.5
I'd compare this game to Star Wars - Epic Duels.  Except you don't have cards to battle with. While I certainly wouldn't call this game overrated, I don't see why it should be so much better in comparison to the referred game. 

1. The amount of luck is the same. With the difference, that luck or misfortune in SWED blasts you or the opponent away within 15 minutes gaming time. Whereas in this game, you'll be by far more frustrated, when misfortune hits you after an hour and a half.
2. Speaking of imbalance: As in SWED there are more and less powerful charakters. With the exception that from some of the "should-be-powerfuls" you get less than what you hoped for. (Speaking of the basic set only)   

Don't get me wrong here! I like this game, it's fun, it looks sweet, but I'd vote for SWED over this one anytime.

RATING: 5.9
5 TO 9!  I'd rate HS all the way as low as 5, and all the way up to 9.  There are all kinds of reasons for both, but it really is a twisting, confusing series of thoughts that I have on this game.  For awhile, it was all I thought about, gaming-wise.  I scoured stores everywhere for specific boosters, driving my poor kids with me (Dad, why are we in K-Mart again?  We never go there, except with you....).  But then, I hit the set-up wall.  And I think I nearly killed it with all the stuff I gathered.  3 masters sets, 1 Marro master set, and tons of boosters.  And to pull it out and set up a game is rough enough.  But then, there is the draft.  I suppose I could go and simply cull out 1 master set for quick games, but man, that seems like a lot of work.  

Bins and tubs and boxes.....

But still, I love it.

:star::star::star::star::star: Variety (Width) Fun derived from trying out a large variety of meaningful paths through the possibility space landscape.
:star::star::star::star::star: Surprise (Height) Fun derived from the experience or anticipation of encounters along a path through the possibility space landscape.

RATING: 6
HeroScape is in an odd position for me. It promises great amounts of fun, and for the most part, delivers.

I only have a couple of issues with it. For one, set up time (including terrain) is *very* long. And second, the sheer amount of stuff to buy is incredible.

Both of these issues, admittably, are my own problems. The first can be solved with more space to leave the game up, and the second is only a problem if, like me, you have a "gotta have it all" mentality.

Good game, but I'd much rather pull out a smaller box that's easier to setup and is still great fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Dec, 09: Great fun, but setup time keeps it off the table as much as it could be.  Wish I had space to leave big built maps setup for days so as to enable quicker play sooner.

Jan, 14:  After four years, I have to bump this up to a ten.  Even though it can be a challenge to get on the table, every single game is nail biting, cheer out loud, palm sweating, fist-pumping fun.  Damn I wish I would have bought more stuff when I had the chance.

Letter Grade: A-.   

Snap judgment: 9.  It's a grand, huge system of a game.  If you assume drafting is a part of the game it adds quite a bit to your tactical considerations.  But once you get stuck into the fighting, the skirmishes are quick and light and fun.  It has a great sense of scale for the playing time.  Only a couple expansions gives you a staggering amount of replay value.  It seems like this game will give back exactly what you want to put into it.  

[05-08-09]: Old Rating: 9.  New rating: 8.  HeroScape is a game that I am obsessed with in bursts.  If I'm not playing it, I'm REALLY not playing it, but if I am, it's all I can think about.  Part of it is the set-up, the hauling out of the parts and construction of the board.  Part of it is the collectibility of it, which is (for my mentality) a blessing AND a curse.  If I had a permanent place to leave this up I'd rate it higher. It's a lifestyle game.

RATING: 7
I finally tried HeroScape for the first time this year as a few friends started getting very into the game and buying the game and many expansions. So my first experience was not only with the base game, but with around 10 expansions thrown into the mix as well. It's handy to have friends that are so into the game because they can take care of the laborious setup before you even arrive, since preparing the map for battle sounds like it takes as long as the battle itself (which reminds me of a series of games about tanks, elephants, and goblins). Unlike that series though, HeroScape was really fun. Sure it primarily revolved around rolling gobs of dice and sure it was essentially playing with little plastic army men, which may explain the appeal in great part due to the nostalgia factor for a long-gone youth spent in large part making up rules for grand army men warfare. But despite all that, or more likely because of all that, it's simply fun. I was actually struck by how much more complex the game is than I had anticipated. The base rules themselves are quite simple, but when you throw all of the many units' special powers into the mix, it becomes a lot to keep track of. We played four-player games divided into two teams of two players each, which I think was a great way to structure the battle. Being a long-time fan of team games, from Nexus Ops to Ingenious to Crokinole, I particularly enjoyed the team game elements of HeroScape when played this way. I found the three-player free-for-all to suffer from the same issue as discussed above regarding End of the Triumvirate and Through the Ages. HeroScape doesn't seem like a game I'm going to start purchasing any time soon, given the space it takes to store and the setup time, but it's one I'll be happy to play, especially if we play a team game and someone else sets up the map.

RATING: 9
Rise of the Valkyrie

Grass, Rock, Sand, Water (Dice and game components)

Mimring, Finn, Thorgrim, Tarn, Agent Carr, Krav Maga Agents, Ne-Gok-Sa, Marro Warriors, Syvarris, Deathwalker 9000, Zettian Guards, Raelin, Izumi Samurai, Sgt. Drake Alexander, Airborn Elite, Grimnak

I have 3 sets of 1st edition (sparkly water) and 4 sets of 2nd edition, plus extra terrain only from ebay. I use only 1 of each figure.

Heroscape is a favorite game of mine, I started collecting Heroscape right after Wave 3 was released (introduced by Craig van Ness at Unity Games 9), and I now have every piece produced, including all promotional figures, duplicates of all commons and terrain sets.  I like to attend heroscape events, especially tournaments. Army construction is key, and how figures interact on a team is most important. You learn by doing, and finding out how powerfully some figures work together turns up some real surprises!

I sold one unopened set on ebay in Dec. 2013 for $175.00

RATING: 8
I finally succumbed to curiousity after years of hearing about this game, and I'm glad I did. This is in no way a serious miniatures wargame, but it allows for quite a range of play styles. It can be simple enough to play with children, or deep enough to occupy a couple of gaming adults for a long afternoon of building, planning, drafting, and playing. And it certainly looks great on the table and has a ton of production value for the cost.

The only reason I wouldn't rate this a 10 is that there's not *quite* enough in the Master Set to entertain serious gamers for more than a few plays. You don't need everything in the Heroscape line to have a great game, but you need more than this. In particular, the lack of common squads and bonding leaves out a big gameplay element. However, for the price ($30-$40 usually), this is still an unbeatable value.

Update 5/08: Dropped to an 8. My enthusiasm has dimmed somewhat, though I still expect to get plenty more games in.

RATING: N/A
This Fantasy Battle Board Game comes with dozens of painted plastic miniatures, each representing a warrior from a different era, and hex-based hard plastic terrain pieces which can be put together in many different ways. The warriors include 30 plastic figures, including World War II soldiers, futuristic robots, aliens, a T-Rex-riding orc, a large dragon, and many more. Each hero or squad has its own card that details both movement and combat abilities.
\13\\13\
The rulebook features two games: a basic and a master version. In the basic version (designed for younger players less than 8 years of age), characters move, attack, defend, and have range -- but there are no special powers and some other rules are minimized and/or eliminated. The master game includes special powers, wounds, engagement rules, falling rules, and a few other additions.
\13\\13\
Combat in the game is fairly straightforward. You roll attack dice as listed on your unit's card (1 to 8 dice in the Master Set), and the opponent rolls defense dice equal to the number on their unit's card (1 to 9 dice). Skulls rolled in excess of shields count as wounds (hero figures may have more than one Life).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Pre-painted minis! Constructable Terrain! Non-collectible! (At least in theory; good luck finding wave one without paying through the nose, but I digress...)

Heroscape is one of those wonderful phenomenons that only comes around every decade or so. Put simply, it's a toy for seven year-olds that is purchased and played with exclusively by thirty year-olds. The terrain is great for wargaming, the miniatures are great for roleplaying, and the rulebook packs a pretty solid game as well.

On the flip side, the small size of most of the tiles (only one or two hexes) makes set-up and take down a chore. Ironic, since building your own battlefield is one of the main selling points of the game! The stat cards are another odd bit of irritation. Why they didn't use a standard card size for sleeving is beyond me. The cards (especially ones packed in later expansion boosters) are awkward, flimsy, and take up way too much real estate.

Everything else about the game is pure unadulterated fun. Movement is simple and intuitive. Combat is a breeze and packs plenty of excitement. Army building is engaging and drafting is even better. The figures all have different special powers that muck with the game's mechanics, yet everything seems to stay pretty well balanced. As my good friend Zxqueb likes to say, "Heroscape achieves it's tremendous gameplay balance by making everything broken".

Runes are the only "iffy" mechanic in the game. They seem to be tacked on and actually do a fairly good job of unbalancing things. Do yourself a favor, and pretend they don't exist...

The kids and I love Heroscape. It's simple enough for a seven year-old to grasp, yet offers enough depth to be played with the grown-ups. Set-up time is a big issue, especially if you can't leave it up for a couple of days after building it. This is certainly a game which functions better if a whole afternoon is set aside for it. Although individual battles usually take less than an hour to play, you will want to battle it out a few more times after spending an hour or so setting up. Army drafting is quick and easy, so there will be very little down time between games. Now go bash face!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
For the unindoctrinated, Heroscape is basically a very simple miniatures war game with 3D terrain, pre-painted minis, no blind boosters, and a universe that draws on warriors from all of history.  The system is dice-heavy, but still allows for plenty of strategy.  Also, it is totally awesome.  

I've read some complaints about the lack of coherent theme, but that, for me, is part of what makes Heroscape so cool.  What's more fun than building an army of robots, Celts and cowboys to take on a dragon, FBI agents and ninjas?  Nothing, I say, nothing!

My Heroscape collection is much smaller than many that are really into it (I have about half of the characters that have been released, one of each master set, and a couple terrain packs).  For a while this bugged me to death, and I [i]had[/i] to get the rest but lacked the money to do so.  I'm pretty much over it now and am happy to play with what I do have, but be aware that despite the fact that it's not "collectable" doesn't mean that you may not get the collect-it-all bug just the same...

For a brief comparison of the two master sets, see my comment for the Swarm of the Marro.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
How is this possible?  A mass-marketable miniatures game?  Well, it is, and it works.  The rules are simplistic but deep enough to give strategic value to both army drafting and clever play.  The game components are simply amazing (great sculpt/paint jobs on the 30 prepainted miniatures, over 70 interlocking plastic terrain hexes, and tons of nice counters, dice, and other goodies).  The only reason I didn't give this one a 10 is the minor balance issues between some of the units (the unit costs are out-of-whack, which can make for unbalanced armies of the same point totals).  Definitely worth trying out, and it's something you can probably even get your non-gamer friends to play.

RATING: N/A
This Fantasy Battle Board Game comes with dozens of painted plastic miniatures, each representing a warrior from a different era, and hex-based hard plastic terrain pieces which can be put together in many different ways. The plastic figures, including World War II soldiers, futuristic robots, aliens, orcs, a large dragon, and many more. Each hero or squad has its own card that details both movement and combat abilities. While games can play quickly can be a long setup time for the terrain.

RATING: 7.5
This is the game that really solidified wanting to host board game nights and having people come over to play games for hours on end. This is the BEST table top game out there, period (SUCK IT 40K and HEROCLIX). The minis weren't random (blind), they were pre-painted, you build any map you want and its 3D, you can draft an army consisting of any genre you want, and you can have any win stipulations you want. You want co-op, you got it, free-for-all? DONE, area control? I gotchu. What's that? You want a campaign, easy peezy lemon squeezy. It is a crime, A CRIME!! that this game was discontinued. Shame on Wizards of the Coast for dropping the ball on something that I would STILL be purchasing today if they were still making it :angry:

Artwork- 7/10
Theme- 10/10
Mechanics -8/10
Fun- 8/10

RATING: 10
When I was a youngin' I picked up this funky looking game called Axis and Allies.  My friends and I had a blast for years, along with all the other Gamemaster games.  I think Heroscape is similar in effort and result for the current generation.  It's a wonderful entry point to the world of boardgaming in general, and wargaming in particular.  My 11 year old son loves it, and even my wife will play.  Only negative is price; the game really doesn't become great until you get into the expansions.  However, the base game is entertaining, and I heartily recommend this title to anyone. You really must be jaded not to like this game.
